< Review>
This may not be the flashiest landmark we visited in San Francisco, but it was one of the most meaningful for me. The building is the one Harvey Milk had his home and shop in during the 70s and leading up to his assassination. The staff is fun and friendly, and they have a lot of things that aren't available in their online store. My favorite purchase was a set of tote bags that I've used pretty much every time I travel.< /Review>

<name>Marie T Fisher<//name><Date>1386355741865< /Date>< Rating>
5< /Rating>
<text>One of only a few retail locations, this store sells HRC branded items (including the coveted "Love Conquers Hate" tees in English, Russian, and Spanish, as well as memberships. It's a great spot to purchase gifts, as 100% of proceeds go back to funding HRC efforts. They also have a great sale rack with $10 tees. But more than selling merchandise, this site is historic. It's located in Harvey Milk's former camera shop, and is below Supervisor Milk's former apartment. There are videos and memorabilia dedicated to Harvey's cause. The HRC runs events out of this location, and all Harvey Milk marches and commemorations start/end here. A historical must-visit site for locals and visitors alike.</text>< pictures>

Love this place. The foam brushes and wax are excellent. You get a mix of quarters and dollar coins at the change machine that can be used at the carwash. I don't like that just of the displays are missing pixels making the remaining time elapsed basically unreadable. I've been here about 5 times since November 2018 and always felt safe and pleased with wash wands and foam brushes. They also have vacuuming services available but I've never used them. The coin dispenser accepts up to $20 bills. Wish it was updated to accept credit cards.

What a Hidden Gem!

I feel like if you don‚Äôt know about this restaurant you probably would just pass by it and never think to stop and try it.

Location: Los Angeles, CA
Tucked away in what feels like residential and easily missed if not paying attention, Located on the Corner.

Parking: Street Parking.

Decor: Very relaxed and welcoming. This place is nothing fancy but very homey feeling. Casual at its best.

Service: 5 stars.
Immediately greeted as I walked in. I‚Äôm not sure if it‚Äôs family owned but truly felt like it. Staff was very friendly and welcoming.

Food: Delicious.
Everything was very flavorful and hott of the stove. I couldn‚Äôt decide what to order so I tried a bit of a few things and it all met my expectations and more. All plates came out to the table at the same time which is how I love to dine.

P.S
So besides the dinning area they have this section off area towards the back in a separate room with one big table for private parities or a big family dinner, it‚Äôs super cool and worth peeking your head in if your curiosity hits like mine lol

If you‚Äôre ever in the mode for Filipino food or never tired it and looking for a place I highly recommend L A Rose Cafe.

Enjoy!< /review>

<Review>Los Angeles continues to surprise me. Having lived here my whole life, and never did I know about such a wonderful place like this, until tonight. I've had Filipino cuisine mostly from people's homes, but it's unheard of, that I find such authenticity of the Filipino cuisine, in a restaurant.. until now.

After many years of success, Lem Balagot's LA Rose Cafe stands as a beacon of culture, passion, dedication, and a precision in customer relations. I dare say, in my experience with Filipino restaurants, this stands currently at #1 for Filipino Cuisine in LA. With years of experience, Lem and his team of exemplary partners bring a smile to your face, delivering authentic Filipino Cuisine that is both warm at arrival and satisfaction guaranteed. With beautiful interior designs and a peaceful atmosphere, it is quiet enough for a casual date with a romantic touch to it. < Review>
Would have been a 4 or 5 star rating if not for the spoiled Chicken Fillet that they served us.

Went there on a Sunday, 9/23 lunch time. We ordered Buchon which was very tasty and the skin very crunchy. Stupid good. We also got Longsilog because it was recommended by friends. It dis not disappoint. If you love garlic you will surely enjoy their tapsilog and their garlic rice.

And yes, our son wanted to try the chicken fillet. But after a bite or two complained that it tasted funky. So wifey and I tried it and it dis have a very funky smell and nasty after taste. I reported it to our waiter who pointed to another guy, probably the supervisor or the manager who asked for the plate. Came back to our table to apologize and explain that it probably was because of the temperature. After marinating the chicken fillet was not stored in the ref that's why it got spoiled. Offered to replace with chicken inasal instead which was a huge serving, a little bit dry but all in all tasted good.

I guess because they replaced the spoiled chicken with inasal they still included in the bill.<//Review>

<user>117287916588389687990</user><Rating>4</Rating><time>1565826434967< /time>< response>
None< /response>
< Text>
We've only had lunch here twice and I was impressed with most of what I sampled, yet both times was somewhat disappointed with my entree.

The first time I ordered the pansit bihon. The only other pansit bihon I've had was in the Philippines (specifically, at the Graceland Resort in Tayabas, which has a fabulous restaurant), and it was quite different. Then again, pansit is a very personal thing for Filipinos and varies widely. My second visit I ordered the beef machado, having previously sampled it. The first time I tried it I loved it: fantastic seasonings, a lively, robust flavor and the meat was perfect: slightly but adequately marbled. My sister had ordered it that time, and I ate half of her order. However, when I ordered it as my entree the second time it came somewhat dry, without the marbling I'd previously experienced. I asked the owner and he said that he uses sirloin for the machado (which is essentially potroast). Sirloin is very lean, so I believe him. The first time I tried it I could have sworn it was london broil, because of the slight but much needed layer of fat on one end. Maybe they should consider using london broil instead: they'd certainly save some money.

Everything else was magically delicious and had nothing to do with breakfast cereals. The lechon was fantastic, the sinigang was marvelous, as were the other items that I can't quite recall.

One strong recommendation I'll make is to not stuff yourself: you WILL want to sample the desserts, which all look fabulous. We had the chocolate cheesecake and nearly died of bliss.<//Text>

< user_id>
110259556555572316628< /user_id>
<Name>Tom Wagner<//Name><time>1504463149908</time>< Rate>
3<//Rate>
< text>
We've only had lunch here twice and I was impressed with most of what I sampled, yet both times was somewhat disappointed with my entree.

The first time I ordered the pansit bihon. The only other pansit bihon I've had was in the Philippines (specifically, at the Graceland Resort in Tayabas, which has a fabulous restaurant), and it was quite different. Then again, pansit is a very personal thing for Filipinos and varies widely. My second visit I ordered the beef machado, having previously sampled it. The first time I tried it I loved it: fantastic seasonings, a lively, robust flavor and the meat was perfect: slightly but adequately marbled. My sister had ordered it that time, and I ate half of her order. However, when I ordered it as my entree the second time it came somewhat dry, without the marbling I'd previously experienced. I asked the owner and he said that he uses sirloin for the machado (which is essentially potroast). Sirloin is very lean, so I believe him. The first time I tried it I could have sworn it was london broil, because of the slight but much needed layer of fat on one end. Maybe they should consider using london broil instead: they'd certainly save some money.

Everything else was magically delicious and had nothing to do with breakfast cereals. The lechon was fantastic, the sinigang was marvelous, as were the other items that I can't quite recall.

One strong recommendation I'll make is to not stuff yourself: you WILL want to sample the desserts, which all look fabulous. We had the chocolate cheesecake and nearly died of bliss.</text>

<user_name>Myk Bautista<//user_name><Time>1447897785898</Time><Rating>4</Rating>< Text>
This place has a fancy edge for Filipino dining. We have the Karinderia style where you just pick your food and the amount of serving and it's ready, but for this place, it's a sit down with a very nice ambiance. I went here after our Hollywood Hard Rock 5K, so I was ready to eat breakfast after my run (since we all deserve it and we all got our medals)
I ordered the TosiLog, which is a combination of Tocino, cured thin sliced pork with sugar, fried rice (sinangag in the Filipino) and Eggs (Itlog) Hence it's To-(cino)-Si(nangag)-Log(Egg). My other friends ordered Tapsilog, Adobo silog and Longsilog. They are all my favorite for breakfast so I would go back and order it again.<//Text>

<Rating>5<//Rating>< text>
I don't even know where to start with this hidden neighborhood gem. It feels almost sacrilegious writing a review for such a secretive little spot. But, the Foodie gods demand I spread the foodie love, so I must!

First of all, if you've never had great, authentic, down-home Filipino food, you don't know what you're missing. The flavors are a wonderful balance between intense yet humble, hearty, yet healthy; in-your-face, without being pretentious. The owner of this restaurant is no different from the menu he has meticulously created, in that respect. He's one of the most likable, humble men I've had the privilege to meet; a real sweetheart. I liked him the moment I walked through the door.

More importantly, the food is delicious enough to satisfy even the most hardened food snob, and it has the acclamations to prove it. This place has been featured in more reviews, articles, and celebrity followings than I care to count. Apparently, even Paris Hilton is a fan.

To break down such an extensive menu would not be doing it justice. Just know that everything you order here is going to be delicious and memorable, whatever pops out at you from the menu when you visit. However, if you want to do it right the first time, you HAVE to order some of those award-winning sweets. Therefore, I highly recommend the oh-so-decadent bread pudding with a side of ub√© ice cream, if you can handle it. It is as delicious as it is beautiful. Another local favorite, recommended by my new foodie friend Spike T., is the Tocino Pork with a side of Garlic Rice. Apparently it's so good he can't seem to order anything else when he comes here alone, despite his best efforts. And finally, the chicken empanadas: I'm sorry to say this as a Hispanic girl, but... our Central American empanadas just don't compare. These little pockets of flavor make your taste buds burst with excitement, and that dipping sauce is truly something else.

If you don't have the time to sit down for a meal or if it's too packed, no worries. They have a pastry case full of their most popular take-home goodies, such as the Ensaymadas, which are these giant brioche-cream-puff-looking things topped with sweet creams, ub√©, & cheese. Their flans and cheese bars are also among the local favorites. You can also order ahead, and they'll have your smorgasbord of flavors ready to go when you get there.

LA is the hub for exotic cuisines from around the world, not to be missed, yet with so many to choose from, it's often difficult to know where to go next. That's where diamonds in the rough like L.A. Rose come in. Hands down, you have to come try this place at least once.</text>

I typically just go here for a solid tocilog breakfast - Filipino cured pork (tocino) with rice and egg. < review>
My friends are always asking me for a recommendation for Filipino food. Tonight, my dear friend brought me to this jewel. There empanadas were really great, perfect ratio of crust to filling. I enjoyed it with and without the sweet mustard that it came with. It's a great appetizer, even though I enjoyed it as a post-entree/pre-dessert.

For my meal, I split two Filipino favorites. My friend and I had the tocino (pork bbq) and daing na bangus (marinated boneless milk fish) with a side of garlic rice with 2 over-the-medium eggs. I enjoyed my tocino with tomatoes and onions, and my daing with sukang na maanghang (spicy vinegar). They offer a different kind of vinegar called pinakurat.

Definitely a must try. The food is reflected upon the friendly service. This is a staple in my places to go!!!<//review>

(Translated by Google) The first time I tried Filipino cuisine, it was amazing. Buchon tasted like a combination of controlled meat and crispy roasted meat. The skin was crispy and the pork melted in your mouth. Chick Inasal chicken was a bit dry, more like chicken breasts, not like chicken legs, but very seasoned. I look forward to visiting again next time.
This is my first time trying Filipino dishes. We ordered Buchon (Pork belly), Chicken Inasal and vegetable stir fry with tofu.

Buchon-üíØThe skin of pork belly was very crispy and meat was very tender and juicy. It‚Äôs perfect with the sauce on the side.

Chicken Inasal-I am a little bit disappointed with the chicken. The chicken leg was overcooked like dry breast...However sauce is good.

Vegetable stir fry with tofu üíØ very impressive for the flavor, a little sour, salty and very tasty.

Look forward to visiting again.

After taking my card info, she informs me that there is an $800 hold on my card if I use a debit card (a lesser amount if you use a credit card). When I told her I was going to check a few other places before making a decision, she told me they could lower the hold to $500.
I walked down to chat with two other companies who did not have available vehicles so I came back to Green Motion to continue with my reservation.

Once I set myself up for a new reservation she states she will be holding my account for $800. I was confused, because she JUST told me she could do it for $500. Her response....."that's only in some cases when my manager feels like doing it". After I asked politely if she could ask her manager, she aggressively picks up the phone, says 1 sentence, hangs up, and tells me he said no and they can only do $800. What was the point of even telling me they make exceptions??

At this point I'm in awe that these people are even maintaining a business but I was late and running out of options.

Long story short, they charged me an entirely new charge (outside of the $105 I already paid online) of $244.22, and held $800....for a one day rental. I asked several times for clarification that my original online payment of $105 would go towards the $244.22....she told me yes so many times, she was irritated that I kept asking. My worry was exactly this.

The only pleasant experience I had was with the gentleman who gave me the keys, the car was clean and nice.

This is the scamming part.....two days later I get another charge for $169.49, and ONE MONTH later I get two more charges of $65.58 and $75.00. That is $310.07 higher than the only amount I agreed to and have a receipt paid for.

When I attempted to dispute the first charge, its exactly the nightmare you'd imagine. The customer service is non-existent, none of their employees are helpful, they have no explanation for why my card was charged and how or when I can speak to someone who can fix it. Thank goodness for Bank Of America and their fraud department. I will definitely be reaching out to a lawyer who specializes in small business Fraud.

DO NOT RENT FROM HERE

This place LITERALLY steals your money!< /Text>

< text>
MUST READ BEFORE RENTING FROM GREEN MOTION
-first of all it was a decent experience. The lady at the check out counter was nice, however it did take 15 minutes of me waiting in line with no one ahead of me. 2 front end counter staff each with one customer. (those customers experience was not as good as mine. One guy was yelling a lot and the other family was having a hard time getting there car, I was scared) the car was clean no problems with the car, it was brand new. the guy at the pick up spot for the car was very nice and polite. Drop off was easy. The guy was very nice. overall good experience there. now the warning.
1- Bring your own proof of insurance. Bring the original copy you keep in your car. it will make your life much better!!!! otherwise they will pressure you to buy insurance!
2- You have a 2 hour window to pick up your car from the time you said you would be there! I was 6 minutes late and they cancelled my reservation made me pay a fee per day to "upgrade my reservation"  because they have a 2 hour cancellation policy. if you are not there within 2 hours of pick up time, consider yourself cancelled. I was stuck on the tarmac in Calgary for 1.5 hours. I was late by 6 minutes. standing in line for an additional 15 minutes put me 21 minutes over. so they got me for another 92.50. in the future call them if your going to be late!
3- Do not get a parking ticket or drive through any TOLLS! they charge an additional 125.00 for each infraction.
4- Drop the car of early more than 1 day they charge you. 27.11 per day.
everything else is the same as any other car rental.

I would compare my experience to buying a car. They love to up sell and high pressure sales whenever possible. I am in the car industry so it doesn't bother me.
read the back of your pre inspection form for damage costs when you pick up your car, eg. scratches, dents, rim rash, windshield repairs. all pretty standard. look very carefully at the car with your pick up guy to protect yourself. write everything down! take pictures or a video of your car just in case.

I would have given them a 5 star if they didn't penalize me for being 6 minutes late. I would have argued if I was on time. but I wasn't. but that should not have mattered. I pre paid in full for the car in advance. Oh well Live and learn.

Hope this helps.</text>

A genius concept and a great experience both for the food and the people watching.
The place is small and crowded but it gets fast turnover and you're seated before you know it. While you wait the entertainment of observing the locals keeps you busy and intrigued.

I‚Äôd heard about this place before, so I was very happy to discover that it is very much so worth the hype!

It was crowded, but we were able to be seated pretty quickly.  You order first at the counter before finding somewhere to seat, and they were very quick and friendly.
One of them then helped find us somewhere to sit and the food was out in just about no time at all!

For the food, we got some of the pork dumplings as well as the pork rice bowl.  I also got a white wine to pair with it, as they offer different wine, beer, and sake.
The dumplings were delicious - crunchy at the bottom and soft and mushy at the top.  I loved dipping them in the vinegar and Chile sauces.  I also loved the rice bowl and the two eggs that cake with it.
There‚Äôs also a lot of healthy options - they have different cold appetizer and vegetable options every day!

The dining area was also very nice - small but didn‚Äôt feel cramped, thanks to a good design layout.  It‚Äôs contemporary and aesthetic inside, very open and clean feeling!

I loved everything about this place!  The food was delicious, the service friendly and efficient, and the ambiance very airy and relaxing.  I look forward to returning and I definitely recommend!<//Text>

<Review>Come for the crab and ambience.

If you come here with buddies or take friends from out of town, this is really the place for it. The rest of the dishes are extremely weak and small portioned with very average to terrible flavors relative to price and what you can get elsewhere in Chinatown. The crab comes in the $60 range, but again, don't come for just the taste alone.

This place is incredible when it comes to ambience. No one is rushing you to leave, dropping subtle hints to gtfo with the check, or ordering more. If you come, eat crab, talk, and use R&G as the platform for conversations with some good friends, it's the best in the city.

If you come hoping to get the best taste in Chinatown and the best dishes, it's really not it.</Review><Pictures>None</Pictures><username>Stephanie Kelly<//username>< GmapID>

< review>
Delicious dishes covered our table corner to corner. It was hard picking favorites, but the pork belly with garlic won that honor. The spicy shrimp dumplings were another favorite. They would have a dedicated picture, but we dived into them pretty quickly. One special we got was the sweet potato greens. They were cooked tenderly with garlic and very hearty. The 3 cup jadori chicken had a nice sizzle to the bite that gently warmed the mouth. Each bite slipped around the mouth as the chicken traveled on a wave of gelatinous sauce.  The sea salt cream jasmine tea was the perfect balance of sweetness. Sips that combined the cream, salt, and sweet jasmine really hit the spot.

Looking forward to my next visit!</review>

< name>
Nicholas Dobkin< /name>
< UserId.>
117872276526090591694<//UserId.>
<Text>The problem that connoisseurs of Asian food often have in introducing it to newcomers is the perceived barriers to entry - strange foods without descriptions, a prevalence of unfamiliar languages, places that are off the beaten path for some - these are the barriers that prevent many not born into the Asian cultures from accessing authentic Chinese cuisine. Pine and Crane then is tailor made to address those issues, making it not just the best Chinese west of Chinatown (certainly the best in Silver Lake) but hands down the best place anywhere to introduce anyone new to Chinese food to its authentic appeal.

From the outside, Pine and Crane seems like a Japanese restaurant with classy, minimalist wood aesthetics but it's actually classic Taiwan/Shanghai, offering staples like pan fried dumplings and beef noodle soup. While quite crowded, the wait staff still allow you to come in and then order before they seat you at whatever spot opens first, alleviating any stress over finding the first space you can. Indeed, the staff as a whole is splendid, some of the best and most helpful you could ask for, being kind, efficient, and helpful with recommendations and information.

As to food, it's definitely quality. I had the pork pancake and beef noodle, which turned out to feature pickle making for a more mainland feel. Is it the best out there? Ultimately I would still take San Gabriel authentic stuff if given the choice (doesn't hurt that most authentic stuff would be a touch cheaper too) but the fact that it competes with the best speaks volumes.

Pine competes on its experience, and delivers cuisine that will be very satisfactory to old hands and sublime to newcomers. But it's the overall dining experience that is both accessible and classy which sets Pine apart and makes it essential for visitations to Silver Lake seeking good Asian food. And if you're new to authentic Chinese, there is nowhere better to start than here - 5 stars~<//Text>< Resp>
None</Resp>

< text>
I came here after enjoying Joy, a sister restaurant of the same owner. Pine and Crane is amazing and tastes like home to me! This is authentic food and it is really well done.

The restaurant atmosphere is casual and it can get noisy during the busy evening hours. I suggest coming earlier; the line gets so long to order, people end up waiting outside!

We ordered an abundance of food: beef roll, zha Jiang noodles, 5 spice bamboo, cloud ear/wood ear salad, minced pork over rice. The Zha Jiang Noodles were not what I was expecting, but since this food is Taiwanese, it could be different than what I am used to in Beijing. It was good nonetheless. The bamboo and wood ear mushroom salad are my favorite salads here and I get them every time. I loved the beef roll; the outside was crispy, the meat was flavorful and not chewy, the veggies were fresh and still chilled. We ended up taking one of the pork buns home and they make great leftovers!

I also tried out their passionfruit shandy which was excellent as well.< /text>

<review>We decided to check out the parent restaurant to Joy on York for dinner. The menu is much more robots and the dishes are pretty light in comparison to most Chinese or Taiwanese spots. Light as in less salt, garlic and oil.

We tried the wood eat mushrooms, bean curd and seaweed for appetizers. All three were good, but we liked the bean curd the best of the three.

For our main meal we had the beef roll, pan fried pork buns, wonton noodle soup, three cup jidori chicken, pea sprouts and mapo tofu. We liked the Pam fried pork buns and mapo tofu the best. The pork buns had perfectly crispy bottoms while keeping the doughy texture of the thick bun and the mapo tofu used med firm tofu and was seasoned with just the right amount of spices.

The restaurant is fast paced as customers are lined up outside. I would recommend coming before 6pm as parking is limited in the area. The staff is attentive and the food rolls out very fast once you‚Äôre seated so come ready to eat.< /review>< time>

<user_id>101680887019881172299<//user_id>< review>
Pine and Crane is a small fast-causual Asian (Taiwanese-Chinese) restaurant in Sunset blvd and Griffith Park blvd on Silverlake neighborhood. I came here to grab a late lunch on a Saturday. Indoor vibe was welcoming. Dining area was spacious, organized with a long community center wooden table. You need to order first at the order counter before being seated. It took me some time because the line was long. It was peak (4 pm) hour and it was crowded. I ordered passion fruit black tea with boba, white rice and jidori chicken. Their utensils/water were self service located at the front counter. The icecold passion fruit black tea was refreshing and deliciously served in a 16 oz thick glass cup with a metal straw which I think was cool and environmental friendly; boba (an extra 50 cents) was sweet soft and chewy ball with gummy-bear like texture. Jidori chicken (chicken, chinese basil, soy sauce, rice wine and sesame oil) was tasty, soft and flavorful and its sauce was thick and a bit too much soy sauce.  Serving was above average. Service was fast. Prices were reasonable and competitive. Street parking only and can be difficult given its on Silverlake area. Staff were nice and professional. Overall I had a good food and dining experience.< /review>

<rate>4</rate><Text>If you don't live in this part of town, let me save you some trouble: Uber and Lyft are your new best friends. Parking is horrendous and finding a free spot would be a rare gift from the gods.

That aside, the space is ample and chill on the inside and kind of nice on the outside, too; sans the urine smell. As you've probably heard, the specialty here is inauthentic Taiwanese food with a hipster twist. I'm not sure this would constitute as street food, but most of it definitely isn't healthy, I'll tell you that much. I'm also not the biggest fan of Taiwanese food, so the flavors didn't pop a great deal for me; however, none of it was actually bad.

The Beef Rolls were pretty darn good- a bit crunchy from those slivered cucumbers, salty and savory from that soy sauce, and hearty from all the meat packed in there.

The Scallion Pancakes here are also popular for a reason. I loved the chewy decadence they offered, and while I'm not technically supposed to have scallions or onions of any kind, the flavor of these crunchy slices was worth a little digestive upset.

The Sweet Potato Fries with Plum Powder may have been the most unique of all my choices. The balance between sweet and salty wasn't quite there, but I get what they were going for; and the flavor certainly isn't something I've had anywhere else. This is definitely one of the more carb-loaded dishes you'll get here, as well.

Finally, I tried their Sea Salt Jasmine Green Tea with a thick head of what tasted like cheese foam on top. The tea was a bit too strong and I could have done without the added sugar, but overall, it wasn't bad. The foam is the best part of this drink, so do the "sexy movie thing" and lick some of it off the top before taking a sip of the tea; makes it ten times better.

As you can probably tell, all I had were appetizers for dinner, but the look of those noodle entrees and soup bowls was too much for me to handle. Bring help/ extra stomachs if you can.</Text><userid>114666193461804491581<//userid>< Time>
1571331482934< /Time>

<Text>A solid find in silver lake. We trekked from our west LA posts to that of silver lake to try this restaurant!! Had been recommended to us by a bunch of people :)

FOOD: You order food/pay and then get seated. We got the beef scallion roll, which had cucumbers and meat inside. The meat to cucumber ratio was even, but I wish it was more mixed rather than the cucumber to one side and the meat to the other because one of my bites would be only cucumber or only meat. The scallion pancake was light and delicious.

THE STARS: Beef noodle soup was SO GOOD. the beef was tender and the soup was so flavorful without being heavy and salty. The noodles were almost udon like, thick and chewy. Lots of bokchoy. Delicious.

They RAN OUT OF CHICKEN :( so when we went on a 1pm on Wednesday we had to settle for the mushroom three cup instead. This was not bad.... the flavor of the sauce was sort of sweet and heavy and the mushrooms soaked up the flavor. After a while though, the flavor
Got kind of tiring--but luckily there's rice to wash your palate.

Ambience: really crowded on a Wednesday at 1pm--that's how you know it's good. The line moves fairly quick, maybe ten minutes of waiting for us.
The bathroom was sort of clean-- one was broken and there's only two so that was sort of disappointing.

The restaurant itself is a very cute date spot but fairly loud--don't really think it's a good intimate date spot but nice place to try with a couple of friends :)< /Text>< resp>

< Review>
It is a hip, communal style restaurant.  The vegetable dishes are really delicious and I think they sell their vegetables as raw produce you can buy by the pound.  The experience is chaotic though.  Its popularity means long lines and you order at the counter before you are seated.  But after you order, a waitress seats you (in contrast to traditional Chinese cafes).  But there isn't really a line to be seated so everyone just kind of crowds together.  I had the pea sprouts (amazing), twice cooked pork (which was good but didn't really taste like twice cooked pork), Dan Dan noodles (again good, but not like other Dan Dan noodles I've had), potstickers (the filling was great, but the wrapper was sort of floury and dry like a tortilla. Didn't enjoy), beef rolls (which lacked the right proportions and also the wrapper was dry and floury and unenjoyable).  The wood ear mushrooms as a cold dish which I love, and a spicy beancurd dish that didn't work.  But the vegetables were so amazing that I'd come back.  The sea salt drinks are great.  Try them!</Review>

(Warning: Young adults from Central Florida in for vacation) There was nothing crazy about the dishes here-- and that‚Äôs great! Although the atmosphere and the appearance of the dishes seemed to tell me I‚Äôd be getting a ‚Äòmillennial froo froo‚Äô experience, I was pleasantly surprised to find the dishes tasted like something I‚Äôd get from a great, home chef‚Äôs kitchen.

LIKE A COMFORT FOOD
At first I wanted another dimension of flavor in my Zha Jiang Noodles (Noodles in a fermented soybean base), I also really liked it because it tasted very simple. This was the recurring theme of all our dishes. I especially loved their side of Seasoned Woodear Mushrooms- I‚Äôm pretty sure it was just sesame oil and peppers. Other comforts came from their Pork Dumplings and Pork Potstickers. Everything was simple yet done very well.

ALSO- IT‚ÄôS A CASUAL ENVIRONMENT DONE WELL
When I saw images of the dishes online, I didn‚Äôt expect that this was a place where you order your food at a counter. During our visit, the line stretched out the door, and every single seat was taken. However, Pine + Crane does the smart thing of doing away with having someone in your party ‚Äòsaving a seat.‚Äô Instead, a staffer finds a seat for you AFTER your group orders at the counter. Based on our visit, nobody waited longer than five minutes after ordering.</Review></record>

< Review>
Pine and Crane is a trendy Taiwanese restaurant that   also has some decent beer and alcohol options, which is rare for a Taiwanese place.  The food here is good and as long as you aren‚Äôt expecting it to taste like you are in Taipei you will be quite happy.

Food: 4 stars
Service/Environment: 4 stars
Value: 4 stars
Recommendations:  Beef roll

The one item you will find on most tables is the beef roll. This is the one stand out item I had here. It is better than a lot of places that I have had in Taiwan. The ratio of scallion, cucumber, hoisen sauce, and beef is really well done.

I would stay away from the three cup chicken. I am really annoyed when this dish isn‚Äôt made without Thai basil. The taste is not right without it. Additionally, there isn‚Äôt the right amount of sugar. This dish should taste a tad bit sweet.<//Review>

This is probably the best order of Â§ßË±ÜËãó (pea shoots) I've had anywhere in Los Angeles. There's just enough garlic, ginger, and salt to make things interesting without covering up the fresh flavor of the pea shoots. The shoots are stir fried just until they're cooked through but still crispy.

The ÁîüÁÖéÂåÖ (pan fried pork buns) feature yeasty, crispy dough and porky filling. There's no soup in them, and the dough might be a little over-proofed, but these are solid.

Êª∑ËÇâÈ£Ø (pork rice) here is rich and flavorful. The one knock might be that the rice itself is a little but mushy. Surprisingly, the bowls of standalone white rice didn't have this problem.

The mussels come steamed in briny broth with bright bites of basil and bamboo shoots. The mussels pair very well with the plain rice, and the simple preparation allows the quality of the mussels to shine.

The mapo tofu isn't as spicy as what you'd find at a Sichuan restaurant, but it's still rich and flavorful.

Taro milk tea here comes with actual (very large) chunks of taro. The tea itself is very good. The taro is a nice touch, but might have been better in smaller chunks. The inside of the larger chunks was dry despite being submerged in tea for over an hour.<//text>< pictures>

<Text>Let‚Äôs just agree that this is the best Taiwanese food spot west of Downtown LA. <review>Parking:
Essentially it's pretty much all street parking. There are some metered and some free. Best to find some street parking on Sunset blvd (even though it's a big and busy street). As long as you are not there at popular times, you should find plenty of street parking. (ie. 5pm on a Thursday night). There are parking spots on the small streets in residential areas but those are very hilly so just be careful if you choose to park there! Another option is there is a 99 ¬¢ store super close by, so you can potentially park in their lot... if you buy something!

Food:
Merging classic Taiwanese flavors with a modern aesthetic, Pine and Crane successfully elevates traditional Taiwanese dishes. I personally really enjoyed the Dan Dan noodles and the beef wrap as there was a great mix of flavors! It was also the perfect saucy consistency, not too dry, not too wet. I've never tried dan dan noodles because they are typically a spicy Sichuan dish and I have no tolerance for spices foods. The dan dan noodles here are not spicy at all which was refreshing. It was I credibly delicious and I would come back for these noodles!! The beef wrap was also really good. Packed with I gradients in a crispy scallion pancake roll. Great side dish to share with others.

The 3 cup mushroom and zha jiang noodles were alright and could use a little more flare. The 3 cup mushroom is marinated king oyster mushrooms. The flavor is very authentic and potent but it lacks variety. This dish literally only has marinated mushrooms (served with a bowl of rice). The zha jiang noodles also had good flavor. But it wasn't too special. There are better zha jiang noodles out there.

The foam green and black teas were interesting. The foam here is almost like a butter whip cream verses the dense sweet foam you see at specialty boba shops. I would not recommend getting it here.<//review>< Pictures>

< text>
This place is a staple of East LA restaurants that I frequent and great if you need a place to take the in-laws. I love the seasonal selection of vegetables and how the types of pot stickers are always changing.

If you eat here make sure you always order a round of scallion pancakes for the table and to douse in the INCREDIBLE chili oil they have. They are crispy, savory, and could make your grandmother who‚Äôs lost her taste buds go wild jumping for joy.

I often order the won ton soup. It is always solid. The Jidori chicken as well or the shrimp potstickers which are delicately wrapped in illustrious pinnacles of flavor. They love garlic at this restaurant so if that‚Äôs not your bag, I‚Äôd order vegetarian. The Jidori chicken can come off a bit garlicky to some but I‚Äôm a fan of its deep and flavorful vibe.

The rice beers are refreshing, service is great.
Get there early there will be a line out the door on any given night.</text>

<Rate>5< /Rate>< Text>
Some people will argue about the merits of the hipster/yuppification of Asian food, saying that it increases the price point and takes away from the comforting-hole in the wall element of foods rooted in culture and community, but Pine & Crane manages to take traditional Taiwanese dishes and elevate/update them into forms that may even be better than the originals in their focus on clean food. Less oily. Organic. And their vegetarian take on three cup chicken that uses oyster mushrooms instead of chicken is fantastic.<//Text>

<name>Fareedha Puhrtleff< /name><Date>1559590557707<//Date><Rating>3< /Rating>< review>
Compared to Din Tai Fung, this place is a quick fix for those cravings. The spicy shrimp wontons were okay, but the dish didn't have the same 'kick' in flavors. It was more subtle and less spicy. The beef rolls had great flavor, but I don't like chunks of tendon in my meat. The dan dan noodles were my favorite because it was the most flavorful, but still not up to par with DTF.

Service was fine. The line was long and only street parking is available. On weekends, there is a farmers market right in front so parking tends to be a bigger hassle. You're assigned seating after you pay/order, which was convenient since this place gets so packed. Don't be one of those people that just sits to save a spot - you'll be told to move.

I would skip their passion fruit green tea and the sea salt jasmine green tea as well. Not worth the hype.< /review>

<review>Wait, a Taiwanese kitchen in the Los Feliz area? You're...kidding, right? It's probably super hipster and priced out to...wait, it's reasonable? Hm.

PROCESS

Park. If you can. It's....not the worst thing ever? Ish.
Walk in. Line up. Grab a menu, and decide what you want.
Order. Pay. As my mother commented, you pay your tip before you even get any service. Take a number.
Get guided to a table. Sit there, and your servers will bring your food out to you.
Eat. Eat. Eat.

FOOD

We got a few items - two beers (!), Shrimp wontons, dumplings, Dan Dan noodles, beef stew noodles, scallion pancake, vegetarian mapo tofu, three-cup mushrooms. The beers - they have IPAs, so yes, they're pretty hipster in some sense. The food - it was all pretty good overall, with the Dan Dan noodles being a interesting take, and the beef stew noodles being honestly a bit disappointing, but the only dish to evoke such a feeling. Everyone at the table felt the beef stew noodles were too, eh, strong? Vinegar-y? I'm not sure.

SERVICE

It seemed a bit hit-or-miss. The cashier was very friendly, and the person pouring our beers, less so. The people who brought out the food were also hit-or-miss, as one asked if we would like plates to share without being prompted, while another seemed annoyed at the suggested that bowls might be needed. You'll have to pour your own waters, grab your own utensils, and whatnot. Also, they'll clean up your plates relatively quickly after you're done with one, leaving you very much feeling like you should leave once your table is done with the meal.

One example - one keg ran out mid-pour, so the cashier said we could get another beer at any point, on the house to make up for that. What happened instead? Another server ran out after one sip, while we were seated, and just filled the beer up. It's not a big deal, since after all, we got exactly what we paid for, but the message seemed a bit odd, and honestly, interrupting.

CONCLUSION

This was a pleasant surprise, and actually quite good. It's reasonably priced for the area, and close to home. It's hard to expect every dish to be a winner, but with a relatively small menu, I think it should be achievable. Maybe I'm too critical. One thing for sure though - if service were a bit nicer or more consistent, I think it'd easily get the five-star win.< /review><date>1545009142422</date>< Rate>
4</Rate>

RatingYay! I'm a fan.	All changes saved

A welcomed addition to Silverlake!  My party of two arrived on a Friday around 7pm, and there was about a 20 minute wait.  The line moved pretty quickly as you first order at the counter, and then they bring the food to your table.

My party of two ordered the Dan Dan noodles, minced pork on rice, and the three cup chicken.  This is a good take on modern Taiwanese food, and the crowded restaurant proved it true.  My favorite dish of the night was the three cup chicken.  The chicken was tender, flavorful, and fragrant.  I wouldn't suggest ordering the Dan Dan noodles as they tasted nothing like the traditional noodles.  The noodles lacked seasoning, and there was not enough sauce to cover the noodles.  It was very disappointing.

But overall, I would come to this place if I were in the area despite being able to find authentic and better Taiwanese food in the SGV.< /text>

<UserId.>101304440753745213410</UserId.><name>Raymond Sutcliffe</name>< Date>
1432282563178< /Date>
<rate>4</rate>< review>
Excellent Taiwanese food with a hip, modern ambiance. The setup of the restaurant was a bit weird, you sit yourself after you order (no saving spaces!) There is a limited amount of seating in the restaurant. There's a few smaller tables against the wall and one large communal table. And you're only allowed to sit outside if you're ordering to go...(not sure the reason for this)

We ordered the pea shoots which were one of the daily vegetable selections. We also got the beef roll, beef noodle soup, and the minced pork rice. Everything was delicious, the minced pork rice was probably my favorite. The beef noodle soup was also quite good; the beef was melt in your mouth tender but there were only 2 pieces :(

They seem to offer a large selection of teas, boba, and taiwanese beer/wine. I would love to come back and enjoy more of their delectable Taiwanese cafe dishes and snacks.<//review>

<Rating>5</Rating><Text>So damn fresh. So damn cute. And so damn good. Walking up the register I was immediately won over by a scene from the kitchen of dough being kneaded in preparation to make fresh noodles. That in itself is a huge indicator of the level of integrity this place likely puts into their dishes. A sign announcing this week's fresh picked produce available for sale by the pound was a second heart throb. The vegetables they prepare are local and seasonal from their Asian farm which is why the availability of vegetable dishes may change daily. I had the panfried pork buns (fine minced pork with a burst of broth when you bite into the bun that has a wonderful crisp bottom), Taiwanese spinach that's saut√©ed with garlic, sesame oil and salt), three cup jidori chicken (tender and prepared with a light but flavorful savory sauce), and the noodles in peanut sauce (just get them. no explanation needed). Very warm and welcoming servers. Plenty of light coming into the space really beautifies the food. It's filling and great to share family style if with a group. <resp>None<//resp><Text>This is literally one of my favorite restaurants in all of LA. The mix of clean yet sleek Japanese bench seating set against the hipster scenery that is Silverlake makes for the perfect friend or family gathering. You'll see a wide range of customers from couples to 3-generation tables. And the best thing of all is the absolutely delicious, authentic Taiwanese food served in a modern way.

The eats:
- taro milk tea: made of REAL taro. Seriously good.
- the cold side dishes: my faves--seaweed, cucumber
- beef rolls: flaky scallion pancake rolled with tasty beef slices. Literally the best dish ever.
- dan dan noodles: sesame sauce mixed with noodles plus crunchy julienne cucumber slices
- minced pork rice: yummy tea egg with pickled radish, stewed minced pork with soy sauce over perfectly cooked rice

I CANNOT wait to be back. I probably could eat here for forever...yes, sorta, kinda, yes definitely.</Text><pictures>None</pictures>< username>

<userid>112998794737911627057< /userid><name>Meggan Kaiser< /name>< time>

<rate>5</rate>< Text>
Good like woah. The format is fun and easy: you walk up (but probably wait in line first), place your order based of recurring menu items and some seasonal surprises (from a local farm!), take a number and go sit. Definitely get the tri-selection of cold appetizers. You can taste them as they're right there at the counter. Just ridiculously delicious and simple. Especially the mushrooms (I think they were marinated woodear?). Loved the spicy peanuts, although I'm not sure if it's worth your stomach space or your money, unless your with a small group. Otherwise I'd pass unless you just really love peanuts and fat. The scallion pancake was divine. Just perfect. Beef roll delicious. Maybe not especially filling...but maybe it's just the right size.

Although I split about 4 things with my boyfriend, we were still a bit hungry and that's not usually the case for us, so err on the side of ordering more, and the fact is that you probably won't regret it!</Text>

<rating>3< /rating>< review>
Great taiwanese food this far west? Shutup. No way.

PARKING- such a nightmare. Try parking far up the hill behind the restaurant. I had to circle for about 10 minutes.

FOOD:
-SPICY SHRIMP WONTONS: Great chewy texture to the wonton skin. Personally, it could have been spicier, but I understand that the spice needs to be toned down the further you head west. Great flavor profile from the spicy oil though.
-BEEF ROLL: Maybe I'm spoiled by SGV, but the beef was severely lacking in this beef roll. My pieces were mostly beef shreds and lots of tendon. Scallions and cucumber dominated the textures.
-DAN DAN NOODLES: Loved this! Good chew on the noodles, and the sauce was on POINT.

DRINKS: Bonus points for offering Taiwan Beer!

TIP:
-This is a fast casual establishment. Get in line, order, sit at a table and wait for your food. You won't need to wait long as service is lightning fast!
-Great takeout option: Lots of people with phone orders.<//review>

<Review>Being from the San Gabriel Valley part of time, I've had my share of Taiwanese cuisine. So when I heard of a new Taiwanese place opening up west of the SGV, I was (and am always) bias about the quality / authenticity of a place before even trying.

Nonetheless, I finally tasted Pine & Crane this past weekend and was satisfied, although I've had better. The flavors and spiciness was all a bit tamed down for the community.

The DAN DAN NOODLES could have used a bit more spice and peanut flavoring. The noodles were done well, though.

The SPICY WONTONS could have been more spicier.

The BEEF ROLLS could have used a bit more beef and hoisin sauce. Too much veggies in the wrap.

The TAIWANESE STICKY RICE was a tad too sweet for me. The balance of savory was lacking.

The SCALLION PANCAKES were probably the best tasting dish compared to what my taste buds are used to and were my favorite. So glad they didn't mess this one up!

Great alternative for community if you're lazy to travel to SGV for the tastier, better quality choices.< /Review><time>1430155126008< /time><username>alice chung</username>< resp>

<text>I was excited to find a Taiwanese place closer to me than SGV.  The interior is really nice.  You basically have to order and then they seat you.  It is a small dining area so I had to wait in line for about 20-30mins.

<time>1453412862513< /time><Rate>4<//Rate><Text>Thanks to my friend for suggesting this place, because I would never in a million years consider driving out to Silverlake for Taiwanese food when it is usually readily available in the SGV. But I have to give props to this place because I was actually quite amazed at how delicious and authentic everything tasted.

We decided to venture out to hipsterville on a Friday night and there was a decent line out the door when we arrived, although it moved pretty fast. The way the restaurant operates is that you first place your order and pay for your food at the cashier, then wait to be seated. The restaurant is small so the place gets packed, but the food comes out at lightning speed so they get you in and out pretty quickly.

We ordered the following items:

-Beef Roll ($6.50)
Cucumber, Cilantro, Scallions, House Hoisin

-Cold Seaweed ($3.50)

-Beef Noodle Soup ($9)
Beef Shank, Baby Bok Choy, Preserved Mustard Greens

-Dan Dan Noodles ($7.50)
Sesame-Peanut Sauce, Chili Oil, Cucumbers, Peanuts

-Alishan "Milk" Jin Xuan  ($5)
Sweet Milk, Light Honey, Toasted Almonds

The portion sizes were smaller than the typical portions you get at other restaurants in SGV, but the ingredients they use are fresh and locally sourced, and the food is definitely authentic Taiwanese. I loved that they don't change the taste of the food to cater to the American palate. The food was not overly greasy or overwhelmed by MSG either so that was much appreciated. There's really not many options for Taiwanese food in Silverlake so I can see how their business is blooming, but for those of us in the SGV, I probably wouldn't suggest driving out unless you are already in the area and craving Taiwanese food.

Tip* Parking is a hassle in this area since there's no parking lots so expect to find street parking nearby.< /Text><pics>None</pics>< Resp>

< text>
I went here on a Wednesday night to grab dinner with some friends.  The restaurant was packed when we arrived, but we were extremely lucky to find an empty meter right outside.  I don't remember seeing a parking lot for this restaurant, so you must find street parking to eat here.

This is one of those restaurants where you order and pay for your food first and then you receive a number to bring to your table.  The line to order food stretched outside the door, so it took around 20 minutes of waiting for us to finally place our orders.  Once we ordered our food, we waited for tables to become available.  It was a bit disorganized and we felt like we were blocking the walkway, but there wasn't anywhere else to stand...

My party ordered:  beef rolls, shrimp wontons, beef noodle soup, dan dan noodles, zha jiang noodles, and a taro milk tea.  We ate family style so that everyone could try more items on the menu.

I highly recommend the shrimp wontons, dan dan noodles, and zha jiang noodles.  The taro milk tea was also delicious had taro chunks and the beef rolls was very fresh and not oily at all!  My friend, however, did not enjoy his beef noodle soup and said that it was very bland.  He also stated that he will never order it again.

Overall, I enjoyed my meal, but would rather go to SGV for cheaper Taiwanese food. I would come back again if I were in the area.<//text>

<rating>4< /rating>< Review>
Being a first generation Taiwanese-born kid whose grown up in neighborhoods in LA suburbs like Rowland Heights, Arcadia, and San Gabriel with frequent family visits to Taipei, I am pretty picky about my Asian food! I was initially skeptical, therefore, of a hip Taiwanese food joint smack in the middle of Silverlake, but oh was I wrong!

You are immediately greeted by the smells of garlic, ginger, green onions and soy sauce as you enter the joint. My boyfriend and I grabbed a menu and caught in line, mesmerized by the sights and sounds and happy patrons choosing down on noodles and three cup chicken and so on. My eyes grew wide as I looked at each item on the menu...Pine and Crane has done a good job of putting Taiwanese favorites on the menu. We ended up ordering the beef noodle soup, the beef rolls, the pan-fried pork buns, the green onion pancake, and garlic steamed pea shoots.

Beef Noodle Soup: The savory red-style broth was delicious and delicate. Pair that with the handmade noodles, tasty chunk of quality beef, a bit of bok choy, and some pickled mustard greens, and my tastebuds were singing!! What I really enjoyed about it were the light flavored of star anise and Chinese five spice.

Beef Rolls: takes me back to grabbing breakfast on the streets of Taipei! The hoisin sauce really ties the beef and cucumber together.

Pan-fried Pork Buns: these were fluffy pillows of pork filled deliciousness! Need I say more?

Green Onion Pancakes and Pea Shoots: these are pretty spot on! The green onion pancakes were fragrant and crispy...I couldn't stop eating them! The pea shoots were delicious to munch on and the garlic was not overwhelming at all.

Though the prices seemed higher than the Taiwanese restaurants out east, Pine and Crane has done a great job of selecting quality ingredients. Whereas I would have felt sick after eating that much food, I was happily full and content. I highly recommend you check this spot out too!<//Review>

< Review>
I should have known that despite having good reviews, getting Taiwanese good in Silverlake wouldn't ever really measure up to the SGV experience. I stopped by Pine & Crane for dinner on a weekend. Parking is a little tough. I ended up finding meter parking and walking.

The restaurant is a self-seating arrangement where you order first, get a number, and then find a table. There's several smaller tables and one big communal tables in the middle. There were also 3 tables outside. The restaurant is on the smaller side.

We ordered the three cup chicken, spicy shrimp wontons and sweet potato leaves to share. We also had a slice of "heirloom" watermelon, which is another fancy word for yellow watermelon. It was decently good but very pricey at $2.75 for a tiny slice. You can get yellow watermelon at a Chinese grocery store for like $1 per whole watermelon.

The food was fairly good but expensive. The portion sizes were pretty small compared to other Taiwanese restaurants and they definite charge a lot more. I did like the sweet potato leaves and shrimp wonton but didn't care much for the three cup chicken. I love the three cup dishes at Uncle Yu's in San Gabriel a lot more.

I would say skip this place and drive a little further to one of the many amazing Taiwanese restaurants in the SGV instead.</Review>
